<div id="review_865955391" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/865955391" />
    <a title="Aparna Singh" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5917974-aparna-singh"><img alt="Aparna Singh" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1533982087p2/5917974.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/865955391?book_show_action=true">Feb 26, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aparna Singh" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aparna Singh" href="/user/show/5917974-aparna-singh">Aparna Singh</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer865955391" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4059846801450730734">First of all, who doesn't like a good looking cover? I know, I know they say <i>don't judge a book by it's cover</i>, and I try not to, but who isn't tempted by a pretty cover? <br/><br/>Guilty.<br/><br/>So, the cover is great. It's all dark and spooky and it definitely drew me in. <br/><br/>Now for the matter <i>inside</i> the book.<br/>The Other Side is a collection of thirteen paranormal stories, written by the two authors. I say paranormal, because, yes the cover and the summary conveys 'horror stories inside', not all stories are horror o</span>
  <span id="freeText4059846801450730734" style="display:none">First of all, who doesn't like a good looking cover? I know, I know they say <i>don't judge a book by it's cover</i>, and I try not to, but who isn't tempted by a pretty cover? <br /><br />Guilty.<br /><br />So, the cover is great. It's all dark and spooky and it definitely drew me in. <br /><br />Now for the matter <i>inside</i> the book.<br />The Other Side is a collection of thirteen paranormal stories, written by the two authors. I say paranormal, because, yes the cover and the summary conveys 'horror stories inside', not all stories are horror ones. Some are pretty spooky, enough to have given me a nightmare or two, but many are tales of the paranormal. From benevolent spirits, cursed beasts, horror-fiction characters come alive for revenge on their author, churails (witches) and psychopaths to killer ghosts with their characteristic <i>feet facing backwards</i> (my personal favorite), you see it all. So, its a pretty diverse collection of paranormal stories, some that gave me goosebumps (I usually read at night) and a few that seemed quite cliche and dragged and made me skim over the paragraphs. <br /><br />The characters seemed relatable and felt real enough. Most stories have a good detailing of the plot and setting that drew me in and had me intrigued throughout. <br /> <br />All, yes all stories end with an unexpected twist. In some cases, the climax with a twist fit perfectly like a lost piece of puzzle finally clicking together and making the story spookier than it already was. In a few others, the unexpected final sentence was like a glass of tepid water poured on a serving of hot, delicious, freshly out of the oven chocolate souffle. Those stories could have done better without the unnecessary addition.<br /><br />Overall, I found The Other Side to be an engaging read. It was a refreshing change from all the full length YA Dystopian novels I'd been gobbling the past year. I would definitely put it in my list of top ten paranormal/horror books (if I sit and make a list that is). A recommended read for all fans of the paranormal genre.<br /><br /><i>Find this and more reviews on my blog <b><a href="http://gopaintbrush.blogspot.in" rel="nofollow noopener">Doodles, doodles everywhere</a></b></i><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4059846801450730734" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer806107174" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3406132892400892843">The Other Side, thirteen stories, thirteen kind of fears, a life on the other side that has always been under scrutiny, never believed under white light of sun. But, this book made me believe in all those fears and that obscure life even while I read it in daylight. <br/>Going by the big names, Faraaz Kazi and Vivek Banerjee, I was particularly sure about the quality that I was banking on, but what caught me unaware was the amount of fear it tugged and steered, plunging into the deep corners of long </span>
  <span id="freeText3406132892400892843" style="display:none">The Other Side, thirteen stories, thirteen kind of fears, a life on the other side that has always been under scrutiny, never believed under white light of sun. But, this book made me believe in all those fears and that obscure life even while I read it in daylight. <br />Going by the big names, Faraaz Kazi and Vivek Banerjee, I was particularly sure about the quality that I was banking on, but what caught me unaware was the amount of fear it tugged and steered, plunging into the deep corners of long forgotten fears that I used to feel while listening to those unsaid and never believed stories of my Nan…<br />As I started with the forewords, as Faraaz had said, look behind if someone is staring into the book from above your shoulders, well, I did the same, much childishly. Not to mention, I was afraid. Then the prologue and the advent of adventures and fear made me switch on the brightest light in my room and occasionally peek here and there.<br />By the end of the book, I was already hearing voices and catching some peripheral shadows, not sure if they even existed.<br />I’d mark it as a must read for all those who don’t believe in the word ‘Fear’ and also for those who have had many months or years of not checking and rechecking under their bed and behind closed doors and curtains. The Other Side exists for sure. I believe. <br /></span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/799308678?book_show_action=true">Dec 25, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ismail Sheikh" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ismail Sheikh" href="/user/show/4835091-ismail-sheikh">Ismail Sheikh</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer799308678" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13642395486511274501">I absolutely love short stories. This book was well put together by the brilliance of Faraaz Kazi and Vivek Banerjee. It is one of the rare co-authored books that proves there is great benefit in unity or rather two minds are better than one. Though this is a national award winning writer's book, I support Kazi in his call as he has done a good job of collaborating with his coauthor.<br/>Like any other short story book, there were ones I liked more than others. I was thrilled to read about the fact t</span>
  <span id="freeText13642395486511274501" style="display:none">I absolutely love short stories. This book was well put together by the brilliance of Faraaz Kazi and Vivek Banerjee. It is one of the rare co-authored books that proves there is great benefit in unity or rather two minds are better than one. Though this is a national award winning writer's book, I support Kazi in his call as he has done a good job of collaborating with his coauthor.<br />Like any other short story book, there were ones I liked more than others. I was thrilled to read about the fact that the stories had a closer connect to India.<br />These 13 tales include some of the most gripping fiction I've ever encountered. Consider, for example, Red Bangles, a story that has blood curdling scenes of necrophilia and beastism. Or The Fateful Night, a story that will leave you gasping for air at the predictable shock of it. Or Possession which I think is a story of resurrection -- with a ghastly difference at the end. The Other Side offers these and 10 more stories that will curdle your blood. <br />A word of caution: Do not read at night. And be sure to sleep with a nightlight on after reading the stories in this collection.</span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer1754512942558037847">I picked this book just like that on flipkart while doing my usual purchase! I guess paranormal is not a genre which I associate with India writers which obviously was the main reason behind picking it up. <br/><br/>It is a collection of 13(guess that also came from the scary number 13!) stories where each one is different from other with a common thread of “other world” binding them together. I must say that the “foreword” is one of the best that I have ever read in any book; it definitely sets the mood/</span>
  <span id="freeText1754512942558037847" style="display:none">I picked this book just like that on flipkart while doing my usual purchase! I guess paranormal is not a genre which I associate with India writers which obviously was the main reason behind picking it up. <br /><br />It is a collection of 13(guess that also came from the scary number 13!) stories where each one is different from other with a common thread of “other world” binding them together. I must say that the “foreword” is one of the best that I have ever read in any book; it definitely sets the mood/tone of the book and you know very well what you will get ahead! <br /><br />Coming to the stories, I won’t say that they were “scary-scary” but they were creepy for sure and almost all 13 stories had moments which gave me goosebumps. I was definitely taken quite successfully by the authors to the locations in almost all stories which I will say is one of big plus for any book/story. Their biggest positive here is forcing us to use our imagination to recreate the scenes in our mind which obviously is most scary. <br /><br />I would rate “Strangers in the Night” highest on the “surprise quotient” and “A Mother’s Love” as the happiest of the lot. <br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11637124200572042521">I remember when we were young, we would gather around our Nani (grandmother) and beg her to tell us horror stories. We would listen with enthusiasm, our young brains taking in all the stories of churails and bhoots. Funny enough, I am still a big fan of horror genre but if it is not about a churail it does not have any effect on me. <br/><br/>Reading "The Other Side" was a similar experience to my childhood days and it even managed to bring about 1 nightmare. I mostly read this book in the night to feel t</span>
  <span id="freeText11637124200572042521" style="display:none">I remember when we were young, we would gather around our Nani (grandmother) and beg her to tell us horror stories. We would listen with enthusiasm, our young brains taking in all the stories of churails and bhoots. Funny enough, I am still a big fan of horror genre but if it is not about a churail it does not have any effect on me. <br /><br />Reading "The Other Side" was a similar experience to my childhood days and it even managed to bring about 1 nightmare. I mostly read this book in the night to feel the stories. Every night after I have had the daily dose of reading, I would switch off the lamp but 30 seconds into the darkness I would desperately look for the switch. <br /><br />The writing style was simple. The scene descriptions were really powerful and easily sent my imagination wild. Absolutely perfect book!<br /><br /><br /><br /> <br /> </span>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('TizQkyxl8P/Yhfn+9T+N49aPRMCZIUDfLjy2k+8LY439NfPNOkcn36SrAaFh4+6gm0Xn0g07NgB1KSgLV6w+2g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

Nar<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText7740555688802757959\" style=\"display:none\">A reimagining of the world-famous Indian epic, the Mahabharat—told from the point of view of an amazing woman.Relevant to today’s war-torn world, The Palace of Illusions takes us back to a time that is half history, half myth, and wholly magical. Narrated by Panchaali, the wife of the legendary Pandavas brothers in the Mahabharat, the novel gives us a new interpretation of this ancient tale. The novel traces the princess Panchaali\'s life, beginning with her birth in fire and following her spirited balancing act as a woman with five husbands who have been cheated out of their father’s kingdom. Panchaali is swept into their quest to reclaim their birthright, remaining at their side through years of exile and a terrible civil war involving all the important kings of India. Meanwhile, we never lose sight of her strategic duels with her mother-in-law, her complicated friendship with the enigmatic Krishna, or her secret attraction to the mysterious man who is her husbands\' most dangerous enemy. There are many legends about this man, but nothing definite is known about him. The famous Bengali writer, Sunil Gangopadhyay has pieced together this interesting biography, The Fakir, based on many legends.\n\nLalan Fakir united people of different communities through his simple songs that expressed love of mankind and of God, without adhering to any particular religious creed or any traditional spiritual school. His simple teachings alienated the orthodox communities of Hindus and Muslims. But, he inspired thousands of simple folk who were attracted by his songs and by his universal message of love and hope.\n\nHis simple compositions have since passed into folklore, and his uncomplicated message attracted people of different communities and bound them together during a time of strife and feudal oppression. But, there is no written record of the life history of this mystic. The Fakir is written based on the many legends that abound about him. The author describes Lalan Fakir as a simple young man whose gift of a sweet voice attracts the patronage of a local landlord.\n\nWhile on a pilgrimage with his patron, Lalu contracts smallpox and is presumed dead. His body is set afloat in the river Ganga. However, the young man is rescued and cared for by a Muslim lady. Due to these incidents in his life, he is considered an outcast by the both Hindu and Muslim communities.\n\nBased on these life experiences, Lalu then learns and amalgamates the teachings of various religions and preaches a universal path that does not subscribe to any traditionally defined beliefs. Then he whispers a few words in your ear and disappears, leaving you picking up the pieces of your shattered world.\n \nAdam Price has a lot to lose: a comfortable marriage to a beautiful woman, two wonderful sons, and all the trappings of the American Dream: a big house, a good job, a seemingly perfect life.\n \nThen he runs into the Stranger. When he learns a devastating secret about his wife, Corinne, he confronts her, and the mirage of perfection disappears as if it never existed at all. Soon Adam finds himself tangled in something far darker than even Corinne’s deception, and realizes that if he doesn’t make exactly the right moves, the conspiracy he’s stumbled into will not only ruin lives—it will end them.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"4054830775329401143\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return false;\">...more<\/a>\n\n    <\/div>\n\n      <div           <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer408142030425173699">"My books are like water; those of the great geniuses are wine. (Fortunately) everybody drinks water"- Mark Twain. <br/><br/>The winner of the 2013 National Debut Youth Fiction Award and also the recipient of the YCOF National Excellence award in Creative Writing apart from being the first Indian author to win the coveted ‘Best Debut (Romance)’ title at the international Goodreads choice awards, Faraaz Kazi</span>
  <span id="freeText408142030425173699" style="display:none">"My books are like water; those of the great geniuses are wine. (Fortunately) everybody drinks water"- Mark Twain. <br /><br />The winner of the 2013 National Debut Youth Fiction Award and also the recipient of the YCOF National Excellence award in Creative Writing apart from being the first Indian author to win the coveted ‘Best Debut (Romance)’ title at the international Goodreads choice awards, Faraaz Kazi has been tagged as the 'Nicholas Sparks of India’ by many and is rated amongst the top male romance writers in the country. <br /><br />Kazi is known for his exploits in the digital marketing world and currently heads an agency in Mumbai. Felicitated by numerous institutes, bodies and organizations alike, Kazi is a well-known name in the social media and literary fraternity. He is fondly referred to as 'The Young Marketer' and operates a revolutionary blog with the same name. <br /><br />Kazi is a fellow member of the esteemed 'Film Writers Association of India.' Truly Madly Deeply, his debut mainstream romance novel is the only Indian book to have seven category nominations in the Goodreads annual readers' choice awards and is also the only Indian book in the 'Top 100 YA Global Fiction' list. Kazi is a voracious reader and counts singing as his second love. <br /><br />You can connect with him here- <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.facebook.com/FaruKazi">http://www.facebook.com/FaruKazi</a><br /><br />You can interact with him here- <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.twitter.com/FaruKazi">http://www.twitter.com/FaruKazi</a><br /><br />Or here- <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.instagram.com/farukazi">http://www.instagram.com/farukazi</a><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="408142030425173699" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
